<a id="t-f9c29ff51b"></a>
## Thread: UNIQUE FEATURES OF ISLAM !!!!!!!!!!!!!! — 1 msgs

### UNIQUE FEATURES OF ISLAM !!!!!!!!!!!!!!

- **From:** BV BV <bv5bv5bv5@yahoo.com>
- **Date:** 2012-02-13T09:15:32-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8e8945f3-d49e-452e-8be8-9e04f97f58ba@w19g2000vbe.googlegroups.com>`

```
UNIQUE FEATURES OF ISLAM

Please forgive us for any disturbance, but we have an important
subject to address to you regarding FAITH, and we Don’t intend to
overload your email with unnecessary messages…
Unique Features of Islam
Uniqueness of the Name
The name for the religion of Islam is much more than just a name
because it expresses a deep spiritual meaning as well as an overall
outlook on life and concept of worship. The word "Islam" is an Arabic
word which means "complete submission to the will of Almighty God".

Other religions are named after their founders, such as Christianity
and Buddhism; after a tribe or ethnic group, such as Judaism; or after
a specific geographical region, such as Hinduism. Islam, however, is
unique because its name represents its outlook on life and reflects
its universal nature. Additionally, the name "Islam" was not thought
up by its followers or applied by other people, as is the case with
the names of other religions, but was revealed by Almighty God. This
name expressed nothing new, because submission to the will of God,
i.e. "Islam", has always been the true religion of God. Due to this
fact, and since the teachings of Islam are straightforward, profound
and logical, Islam is the "Natural Religion" of all human beings. The
name of no other religion carries any significant message, or conveys
the true sense of its outlook on life, as does the name "Islam".
Universality & Continuity of the Message
The command to worship none other than Almighty God and to submit to
His will has been revealed by God to all of His prophets throughout
mankind’s long history. The pure essence of the beliefs and teachings
that were revealed by God to the Prophet Muhammad are the same as God
taught to Abraham, who was one of the earliest and greatest prophets.
So actually, Muhammad is the final prophet of Islam — not the first.
Additionally, Islam is the true "religion of Abraham", because Abraham
completely submitted himself to the revealed will of Almighty God.
Islam is truly unique among the religions of the world because it is
addressed to all of mankind. The scripture of Islam, called the
Qur’an, repeatedly addresses all human beings by saying: "O mankind!"
Additionally, in the Qur’an, Almighty God is never addressed as the
God of a particular people or nation. From the very beginning of the
mission of Prophet Muhammad, his followers came from a wide spectrum
of individuals — there was Bilal, the African slave; Suhaib, the
Byzantine Roman; Ibn Sailam, the Jewish Rabbi; and Salman, the
Persian. Since religious truth is eternal and unchanging, and mankind
is one universal brotherhood, God’s revelations to man have always
been consistent and universal. Submission to the will of God, and
worshipping Him alone without intermediaries, has always been the only
religion acceptable to Almighty God.
A Straightforward Concept of God
Unique among the religions of the world, the concept of God in Islam
is completely based upon Divine Revelation. Not only is the concept of
God in Islam characterized by purity and clarity, but it is also not
marred by myths, superstitions or man-made philosophical ideas. In the
pure and straightforward teachings of Islam, Almighty God has clearly
revealed His unique nature and qualities to man in the way which He
wants them to be understood. While other religions have either mixed
man-made doctrines with divine revelation, or ignored the divine
revelation almost completely, Islam’s concept of God is based totally
on what God has said about Himself. Islam’s concept of God can be
called pure and straightforward because there is a clear distinction
made between the Creator and the created. As such, there is no
ambiguity in divinity — it is made clear that there is nothing divine
or worthy of being worshipped except for Almighty God. In Islam,
calling someone other than Almighty God "Lord" or "Savior" is
completely prohibited because such terms compromise God’s uniqueness
and because all of our trust should be put in Almighty God — who is
the Most Merciful and the Controller of all affairs. The only Creator
— Almighty God — is Unique, Eternal and Transcendent above His
Creation. Everything else besides Almighty God — meaning anything that
you can see or even imagine — is part of God’s creation, and thus not
worthy of worship. Almighty God, as He has described Himself in the
Qur’an, is Absolutely One and "the Most Merciful of those who show
mercy". Even though God is transcendent above His creation, due to His
infinite Mercy He is constantly involved with the affairs of His
creatures. Even though God is infinite, unique and incomprehensible,
in the Holy Qur’an He has revealed Himself in a way suitable to the
finite and limited human mind. By reaching out to man and sending
revelations through all of His prophets, God has allowed Himself to be
known through His unique and most-beautiful attributes. Because the
concept of God in Islam was sent by God specifically for mankind, it
appeals to the innate nature of the human being. Due to this fact,
Islam does not ask man to accept irrational, ludicrous or man-made
doctrines about God. The Islamic concept of God strikes a unique
balance between various religions an because is avoids reducing God to
just being some remote and impersonal "First Cause" or "Higher Power",
while on the other hand it also teaches that a direct and personal
relationship with God can be maintained without believing God to be
like His creation or incarnate in it.
Direct Relationship with God
In other religions, even the ones which claim belief in "One God",
people often approach God through an intermediary, such as a saint, an
angel, the Virgin Mary or Jesus. However, it is only in Islam that a
person is required only to pray to God. Some people also nullify a
truly proper and direct relationship with Almighty God by mistakenly
believing that they have a special relationship with Him simply
because they are members of a certain ethnic group, tribe or "chosen
people". Additionally, in Islam there are no priests or clergy — each
worshipper, man or woman, has a direct relationship with their
Merciful Creator — Almighty God. Since God is the Owner and Sustainer
of everything, as well as the only one who can provide true and
complete forgiveness, it is completely futile to try to approach Him
through anyone else. According to the teachings of Islam, praying to
or worshipping anything or anyone besides Almighty God is the greatest
sin a person can commit. Even though other religions believe in God,
they nullify this belief by making the grave mistake of not always
approaching Him directly. Some religions even go so far as to say that
human beings, due to their sinfulness, cannot approach God without an
intermediary — which mistakenly implies that God is unable or
unwilling to forgive human-beings directly. Islam teaches that
Almighty God has the power to do all things and that no one should
ever despair of His mercy. According to the teachings of Islam, God is
always ready to bestow His abundant Grace and Mercy on anyone who
turns to Him in repentance. Even people who used to commit the worst
sin of worshipping others besides God will be forgiven if they realize
what they are doing is wrong and repent. Having a direct relationship
with God, and understanding that He alone deserves worship and praise,
goes hand-in-hand with the Islamic concept of God. This is because
once a proper concept of God is established in the heart and mind,
submission to God and complete reliance on Him alone comes naturally.
Unique Concept of Worship
According to the teachings of Islam, everything that a human being
does with the pure intention of pleasing God is an act of worship. Due
to this, Islam has an all encompassing concept of worship unlike any
other religion. Almighty God has revealed in the Holy Qur’an that His
purpose for creating human beings was to worship Him and Him alone.
Like other religions, Islam has required acts of worship, however
worship in Islam is not limited to rituals. Since Islam is an all-
encompassing religion with guidance for all aspects of life. almost
every action in a Muslim’s life becomes an act of worship if it is
done to build a better relationship with God. Since man’s purpose in
life is to worship and submit to God, worship in Islam has been
defined by God Himself in an all-encompassing way. This is special
uniqueness can also be seen in the fact that most other religions only
require formal worship once per week, while Islam requires it five
times a day. Even more importantly, all rites of formal worship in
Islam are based on Divine revelation, while the modes of worship in
other religions are a mixture of Divine revelation, man-made
traditions, opinions of clergymen and religious councils.
Additionally, in Islam acts of worship such as prayer and fasting have
been described by God and His Prophet in such detail that it gives
human beings a feeling of assurance that the way they are worshipping
God is pleasing to Him.
Based on Authentic Sources
The preservation of the scripture of Islam — the Holy Qur’an — is
unique among world religions. No other religion has a scripture which
is both as old and as well-preserved as the one possessed by Muslims
today. Even scholars who are hostile to Islam admit that the Qur’an
that exists today is exactly the same as the one that existed in the
time of the Prophet Muhammad. Even though many people mistakenly
assume that the Qu’ran was written by Muhammad, it is actually the
literal Word of God. Not only was Muhammad known by his people to be
unable to read and write, but the Holy Qur’an clearly and repeatedly
exclaims that it is from Almighty God – the Lord of the Universe.
Unlike other religions, the followers of Islam have always considered
their scripture to be the Word of God in toto. The scriptures of other
religions are made up of writings that were not considered to be
scripture until many years after they were written – the letters of
(St.) Paul are a good example of this. Additionally, the Holy Qur’an
has always been in the possession of the common believer, and as such
was circulated very widely. In this way, Muslims know that their
scripture is authentic, unlike other so-called "scriptures" which are
still claimed to be scripture even though their authors are unknown.
The Qur’an also remained pure and authentic because unlike other
scriptures, it was written down and memorized in the lifetime of the
prophet that it was revealed to. Also, its wide circulation prevented
scholars, clergy and religious councils from deciding what should and
should not be part of the scripture — since it was already in the
hands of the people in its complete form. It has always amazed people
to find out that the entire Qur’an was not only memorized word-for-
word by hundreds of the companions of Prophet Muhammad, but that it
has been memorized verbatim by thousands upon thousands of people
until this very day in its original language of Arabic. It was only
natural for Almighty God to preserve the scripture revealed to Prophet
Muhammad, because he was the last Prophet and Final Messenger of God.
In short, the Qu’ran is a unique scripture that has come down to us in
its original form and unique language. Due to its pristine teachings
and unquestionable authenticity, the Qur’an removes the need for man
to wonder for himself how to worship and please God, since God Himself
has clearly described these things.
An Eternal Message
Islam has just as much meaning and is just as applicable to people
living in today’s "modern world" as it did for people living 1400
years ago. Since the message of Islam is eternally true it is also
very robust, and as such still has a strong spiritual impact on
millions of people living in the world today. The Pure Monotheism of
Islam, as well as its universal brotherhood, strong morals and
positive outlook on life, is still very relevant and meaningful to
modern man. The continued relevance and applicability to both the
spiritual and worldly life of human beings from all around the word is
just one of the many proofs of the Divine origin of the message of
Islam. Unlike the teachings of other religions, the teachings of Islam
don’t need to be updated or watered-down in order to appeal to a human
being living in today’s troubled world. Since the teachings of Islam
are both spiritually true and eternally practical, they can be lived
and implemented in the daily life of a person in order to make their
life more fulfilling. In short, unique among world religions, Islam
has not had to sacrifice its integrity in order to be both applicable
to "modern life" and to have enough spiritual impact to change
people’s lives.
A Complete Way of Life
Islam not just a "religion" in the traditional sense, because it is
not just confined to acts of worship, morality and other aspects of
personal piety. The teachings of Islam, even though they do cover
religious rituals and morality, also encompass all other aspects of
life. The Prophet Muhammad’s mission encompassed not only spiritual
and religious teachings, but also included guidance for such things as
social reform, economics, politics, warfare and family life. Thus due
to the diversity and success of Muhammad’s mission, Muslims have clear
guidance from God and His Final Prophet on all aspects of life. This
goes hand-in-hand with the Islamic belief that Almighty God does not
leave human beings without guidance in their daily lives — thus His
guidance is all-encompassing. Due to God’s wisdom, and because Islam
is the final revealed religion, the guidance that God has sent is
applicable for all times and for all places. This can be seen in the
fact that the guidance for some aspects of life is much more broad and
flexible than others. Additionally, in the Qur’an, Almighty God has
revealed to mankind that the purpose of our creation is to worship and
remember God in all aspects of our life, and to follow His guidance in
everything that we do. Thus Islam does not accept a secular view of
government and society, but only one based on the Law of God. Nor does
Islam leave it to human beings to decide what is right and wrong, good
and bad, moral and immoral based on their whims, desires or man-made
idea. In short, Islam does not teach people to "Render unto Caesar the
things which are Caesar’s" because, according to Islam, everything
belongs to God. Like all of its other teachings, Islam’s view of other
religions is balanced, realistic and moderate. Islam doesn’t view
other religions as being either completely true nor completely false,
but believes that all true religions were at one time divinely
revealed. However, over time the teachings of the various religions,
due to a variety of reasons, have become distorted and mixed with made-
man ideas. But nonetheless, Muslims are required to be tolerant of
other revealed religions since the Qur’an clearly says: "Let there be
no compulsion in religion".
Moderation
The teachings of Islam, since they are divinely revealed, are balanced
in all of their aspects. Even though Islam is an all-encompassing way
of life, it preaches moderation and rejects extremism. On the one
hand, Islam does not preach complete rejection of all worldly
pleasures in view of the life hereafter; and on the other hand it does
not teach that earthly life is just for pleasure and enjoyment. In
Islam, wealth and worldly pleasures can be partaken of in this life as
long as they are enjoyed in a way that is in obedience to God.
However, Muslims are taught to keep in mind that the life hereafter is
their ultimate goal, and therefore one should be charitable and not
become too attached to worldly things. By maintaining a balance
between man’s spiritual and physical needs, the teachings of Islam are
best suited for the needs of human beings in particular and society in
general. Since Islam is based on clear guidance from God, it rejects
all man-made religious excesses, such as certain forms of monasticism
where people try to completely "reject the world" and other forms of
extreme self-denial. Islam teaches that human beings have
responsibilities at all levels — to other individuals, to their
families and to society as a whole. By maintaining a unique balance
between the physical and spiritual, and between the individual and
society, Islam maintains a balance in all directions.
A Positive Outlook
Most people will agree that having a strong self-esteem and a positive
outlook on life is conducive to achieving happiness and success.
Unique among the religions of the world, Islam’s view of both the
nature of the human being and the purpose of life are extremely
positive. Islam’s view of the nature of the human being is balanced.
On the one hand they are not viewed as being inherently evil, but on
the other they are not considered to be perfect – nor are they
expected to be so. According to the teachings of Islam, every human
being, man or woman, is born with a clean slate and is equally capable
of both good and evil. Since God has bestowed limited free-will on
human beings, they will ultimately be held responsible for their
actions. Believing that "salvation" is based on "faith alone" reduces
human life to a near meaningless and fatalistic existence. The
teachings of Islam make it clear that human beings, since their nature
is basically good, are capable of positive action in this life, and
that the best way to achieve a balanced, happy and fulfilled life is
complete submission to Almighty God. Certainly, no person can
completely submit to God by simply wanting to do so, but by first
realizing that none has a right to be worshipped and obeyed except for
Almighty God, and then making a reasonable effort to follow God’s
commands, all human beings can fulfill their reason for existence –
which is to worship God alone. . The Holy Qur’an tells us that "man
was created weak" and thus falls into sin often. On the other hand,
man is not to think of himself as so evil and corrupt so as to despair
of God’s mercy. As a recourse to this, and since Islam condemns self-
righteousness, a pious life can only be lived by trusting in God —
since there is no power or strength except through God. As such,
spiritual felicity is achieved by a combination of both faith and
action. As such, the most righteous person is not one who thinks that
repentance is unnecessary, but the one who admits and realizes his
mistakes – and then repents. According to the word of Almighty God as
revealed in the Holy Qur’an, mankind is God’s trustee on earth; and as
such the life of this world is a test, not a punishment. Even before
God created the first man, He knew that he would sin, however God
created man in spite of this. According to the Qur’an, God has
bestowed on human beings a great trust and given them dignity. It is
only by worshipping Almighty God, directly and without intermediaries,
that a human being can fulfull their true innate nature and purpose of
existence. In short, Islam is realistic. It portrays human beings just
as they are and the life of the world just as it is. Since the outlook
of Islam is divinely revealed is not based on wishful or negative
thinking, but simply on reality. Islam also has a positive view of
mankind in general, since it teaches that the best person in the sight
of God is the one who is most God-conscious. In this way the truth of
Islam and the universality of God’s message transcends all of the
barriers of race, nationality, ethnic group and economic status.
————————————–

## Thread: Strange file. — 11 msgs

### Strange file.

- **From:** drop dead google <foodman123@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-02-15T09:51:44-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c89d420d-7c3c-4ec0-8576-767744a1a468@eb6g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>`

```
Hello:

I have a simple program which writes a LINE-SEQUENTIAL file.  The
records are 100
characters.

After the file has been created, the program calls another program
which
displays the records in the file.

There are 16 physical records in the file.

When the file is displayed, it displays as though there were 15 blank
lines in between each valid line.

I found that the program which displays the file actually does 256 (!)
READs to that file each returning a FILE-STATUS of zero even though
there
are only 16 records.

Looking at the file with BRIEF, I found that each record is actually
4,100 characters in length and that characters 101 through 4,100
contain a character which looks like a U but with square corners, like
a rectangle with no top line.  I emailed BRIEF and Paul said that the
character displayed is used when the byte contains something not in
the code-page.

I emailed the EXE to another of my PCs and the program does the same
thing there.

Any ideas, anyone?

Tony Dilworth
```

So go find out why your program is writing 4000 characters more than it should. Perhaps if you

Why would you expect it to behave differently?

Your program that writes the file is broken. Fix it.

Seriously -- that's where the problem is. Your program is writing crap into the file. Without seeing the 
code, it's not possible to tell how, where, or why, but it's clear that the program which creates the file 
is at fault.

From the small amount of source code provided I can see two errors:

1)    'LINE-SEQUENTIAL' should be spelled 'LINE SEQUENTIAL'

2)    'FILE-STATUS' should be spelled 'FILE STATUS'

If you were to provide more of the source code then we may be able to
point out other items which may be relevant.

It would also be helpful if you would provide the environment that you
are using (MS-DOS?) and the compiler.

Using a hex dump would show what those characters actually were. It
would just be a guess but they may be NULLs (hex 00).

#### ↳ Re: Strange file.

- **From:** Alistair Maclean <alistair.j.l.maclean@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-02-15T13:05:13-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<fbaf3351-991e-4f95-99cf-8c16a4eab0a4@hb4g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Feb 15, 5:51 pm, drop dead google <foodman...@gmail.com> wrote:
> The records are 100 characters.
>
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Is it a coincidence that 16 physical lines X 16 lines displayed = 256
reads?
Your first program is writing out a physical record of 4100 characters
where only characters 1 to 100 are properly populated either because
the creating program has a mis-stated RECLEN (of 4100) or because you
are writing one good record and 15 records of rubbish for each
intended good record  written.

Either change the first program to cut the RECOLEN to 100 or change
the second program to read a RECLEN of 4100.
```

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9q3840F5vdU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Alistair Maclean wrote:
> On Feb 15, 5:51 pm, drop dead google <foodman...@gmail.com> wrote:
>> The records are 100 characters.
…[27 more quoted lines elided]…
> the second program to read a RECLEN of 4100.

It is supposed to be a LINE SEQUENTIAL file, Alistair. That means variable 
length records, usually terminated by a CR/LF. (Although the terminator can 
be platform dependent)

Doing what you suggest would make it a FIXED LENGTH record. (recording mode 
is 'F'... if memory serves...).

There are obvious COBOL errors in Tony's code so it is unlikely that what he 
has posted was actually cut from the REAL code

Beside, RECLEN doesn't mean much outside of the mainframe; I can't think of 
any PC utilities that use this parameter.

On Planet Foodman (where Tony lives...) the Laws of Physics (and of COBOL) 
may well be whatever Mr. Dilworth wants them to be.

He has a novel approach to using COBOL and it works for him. He has stated 
previously in this forum that he won't employ anyone who doesn't "get" his 
approach so he probably doesn't have a large pool of people with experience 
of standard COBOL debugging techniques that could help him solve this 
problem.

It seems pretty obvious to me that this could be easily solved with a Hex 
editor (to see what's going on) and a copy of the COBOL standard syntax (to 
make sure the code complies with what is needed for LINE SEQUENTIAL file 
implementation.)

Pete.
```

I use setedit http://setedit.sourceforge.net/

It does syntax highlighting and is configurable. Here is the bit that
you would add to /usr/share/setedit/syntaxhl.shl


# ---------------------- Cobol ----------------------
# Contributed by: riplin
#
Name=Cobol
Files=cbl,CBL,cob,pd,ws,fd,sa
Case=0
AllowedInsideNames=-
EOLComment1=*
EOLCInFirstUse1=1
EOLComment2=*>
Symbols1=+-/*=<>&.
Symbols2=()[]
String1="
String2='
NoChecknumbers=1
HexMarker=0x
PMacros=cobol.pmc
Preload
Keywords=accept,access,acquire,actual,add,address,advancing,after
Keywords=all,alphabet,alphabetic,alphabetic-lower,alphabetic-upper
Keywords=alphanumeric,alphanumeric-edited,also,alter,alternate,and

of other languages and highlights and colour codes accordingly. It has 
features which other Editors SHOULD have...:-))

## Thread: OT:The debate heats up — 1 msgs

### OT:The debate heats up

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-02-18T00:50:18+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9q6t7rFa1eU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
We have already had some comments here about whether it is desirable or not 
to have a PC look like a mobile phone, and vice versa.

I'm currently looking again at phone development using Metro (it is really 
very interesting...), and this will be the same interface for Windows 8.

Whether you think a bicycle should have a different user interface from a 
car, or whether you think it would be really cool if they were the same, 
there are arguments pro and con.

I enjoyed this article and particularly the comments on it.

Hope you do too... :-)

http://allthingsd.com/20120216/apples-mountain-lion-and-microsofts-windows-8-both-aim-to-make-desktop-more-like-mobile/

It will indeed be interesting to see how this pans out.

Pete.

## Thread: COBOL for sale? — 3 msgs

### COBOL for sale?

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-02-21T11:38:57+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9qg0c5F4kgU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Does anyone have or know of anyone who has, an old version of Fujitsu 
NetCOBOL they would be prepared to sell?

This is the bog standard native code for Windows version of the compiler; I 
do NOT want copies of the CIL generating NetCOBOL for .Net.

I am looking for any version from v6 or above.

Don't need PowerCOBOL, PowerForms, or any utilities; am only interested in 
the NetCOBOL compiler and IDE (which is provided through PowerGem).

If you can help, please contact me privately.

Cheers,

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL for sale?

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-02-20T17:36:54-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<e6c6bbf1-a8e9-4f1b-bed5-f05af2eb81b0@oy2g2000pbc.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<9qg0c5F4kgU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
On Feb 21, 11:38 am, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:

> Does anyone have or know of anyone who has, an old version of Fujitsu
> NetCOBOL they would be prepared to sell?
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> the NetCOBOL compiler and IDE (which is provided through PowerGem).

NetCOBOL 6 is 'protected' by a licence number and the need to get a
'key' from the Fujitsu (or some other) server. Given that 6 was more
than a decade ago, it may be difficult to get a usable key, especially
if you aren't the registered owner.

It is possible to move the key from one working machine to another,
but it needs to initialize the move media on the destination and then
write the key on the original (which disables that copy) before
putting the key onto the new copy.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: COBOL for sale?

- **From:** dashwood@enternet.co.nz
- **Date:** 2012-02-20T21:28:24-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6c0f2ce9-be7f-48ab-b3cf-adcd75dd4501@qs5g2000pbc.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<9qg0c5F4kgU1@mid.individual.net> <e6c6bbf1-a8e9-4f1b-bed5-f05af2eb81b0@oy2g2000pbc.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Feb 21, 2:36 pm, Richard <rip...@Azonic.co.nz> wrote:
> On Feb 21, 11:38 am, "Pete Dashwood"
>
…[20 more quoted lines elided]…
> putting the key onto the new copy.

So that would be a "no", then? Gee, thanks for your help...

(It is possible to transfer a v6 (or any CASPER based licence key) to
another party/machine, and I am fully familiar with the steps needed
to effect this.)

Pete.
```

## Thread: Google Groups relay of this Usenet group — 54 msgs

### Google Groups relay of this Usenet group

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-02-21T12:59:04+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9qg527F7abU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Today I had occasion to access this newsgroup through Google Groups as I was 
testing the link from the COBOL21 site to this group.

I was quite apalled at the amount of OT rubbish that is being posted and NOT 
filtered by Google.

Because I usually access via a Newsreader (Outlook Express) I don't see all 
the exhortations to convert to Islam or the fact that somebody is doing some 
kind of jiggle in a Bollywood movie.

My Newsreader filters all the rubbish and also allows me to add filters for 
posts I don't want to read.

I'm not sure what percentage of readers here use Google Groups to access and 
would appreciate it if some who do could indicate that.

Perhaps it may be possible to get Google to implement some basic SPAM 
filtering, if it can be shown that a number of people use Google to access 
this group?

Alternatively, it may be possible to set up a relay where we can filter it 
ourselves.

Comments? Thoughts? Ideas?

Pete.
```

I am unaware of anything which exists to prove otherwise, Mr Brazee, and 
would be interested in seeing documentation showing the improvement of 
said students.  

That Socrates was written of as answering questions with questions does 
not make anyone who answers questions with questions a Socrates; to don 
the robes and methods of an Ancient does not make one the equal of an 
Ancient.  As attributed to Carl Sagan, 'They laughed at Columbus, they 
laughed at Fulton, they laughed at the Wright Brothers.  But they also 
laughed at Bozo the Clown.'

As for Socrates...  have you read Xenophon's portrait?  My recollection is 
that it differs substantially from Plato's.

(I believe it was Macauley who said 'The more I read of Socrates, the less 
I wonder why they killed him.')

DD

> 
>> > Having looked at the web site you provided, it seems their
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
> 
The main point of the Usenet Improvement Project is that Google's interface attracts large numbers 
of two groups: people who have no clue how Usenet works, and spammers -- and Google has no 
interest in educating the former, or doing anything to stop the latter. 

Usenet would be a vastly better place if sysadmins the world over would configure their 
newsservers to automatically drop all posts originating at googlegroups.com. Then the gropers 
and the spammers could talk to each other, and not bother the rest of us.

The term 'interface' as I have used and understood it to
be is the user interface [to usenet]. You appear to be
referring to some other 'interface'.

The following is why I understood user interface.

< http://twovoyagers.com/improve-usenet.org/ >
-----
If these Google Groupers were using proper news clients, some
of them might have a chance at becoming clued themselves; but
clinging to Google Groups prevents this. It doesn't help that
the Google Groups interface (which grew out of the infamous
beta of 2005, which as of August 2006 was reclassified as as
non-beta) is now worse than their original one. Update,
Spring 2007: That wasn't bad enough; now they've downgraded
further to another new version and it seems to be in a continual
state of continued degradation.

There is an excellent short article about these issues here.
Please read it.
-----

The 'here', above, is a link to
< http://al.howardknight.net/msgid.cgi?ID=120829004500 >

On Sat, 12 Apr 2008, Maxwell Lol wrote:

> bz <bz+na...@ch100-5.chem.lsu.edu> writes:
>
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>
But the issue isn't just spammers.

When "google groups" was just the Usenet archive (and the ability to
post), it did not seem to be a problem.

But then they added their own "groups" and that confused things,
and likely brought in a bigger user base that was interested in
only "web forums".  That "google groups 2" interface was very much
in favor of their own groups, things like no automatic quoting of
what you are replying to, the hiding of email addresses (when it's
far simpler to use software connected to a real newsserver to collect
email addresses if that's what you want to do, than process their
webpages), the lack of distinction between their groups and the Usenet
newsgroups they archive.

On Feb 22, 8:09 am, Doug Miller <doug_at_milmac_dot_...@example.com>
wrote:
> Rick Smith <rs847...@gmail.com> wrote innews:491eced4-3688-4863-90c8-85c414a4c308@p12g2000yqe.googlegroups.com:

> breaks in my post, when you quoted it.

After spending far too much time, I identified three cases
where text was mangled and one similar combination were it
wasn't.

In those cases where the sequence was Miller->Smith->Miller,
or ES->GG->ES, the result was Original->Quoted->Mangled.

In the case of ES->GG->not ES, the result was
Original->Quoted->not Mangled.

This suggests the problem is on the ES side.
```

```
On Feb 23, 2:09 am, Doug Miller <doug_at_milmac_dot_...@example.com>
wrote:
> Rick Smith <rs847...@gmail.com> wrote innews:491eced4-3688-4863-90c8-85c414a4c308@p12g2000yqe.googlegroups.com:
>
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
> breaks in my post, when you quoted it.

The line breaks aren't mangled when they are quoted, the mangling is
in the original message from you. In the original message there is a
line feed after the word 'line'. As I am viewing this in a column that
is less than the full length of that line it is wrapped to fit the
column after the word 'it'. If, as would be normal, the whole
paragraph did not have any control characters (eg LF) then the
wrapping would fit correctly in any column width and no 'mangling'
would occur, even when quoted.



> > With the understanding that I would not be part of 'us'. <g>
>
> That, of course, is entirely by your choice. There are many alternatives available, at no cost, that
> work far better. If you choose not to use them, that's up to you.

```
On Feb 22, 7:26 pm, Doug Miller <doug_at_milmac_dot_...@example.com>
wrote:
> Richard <rip...@Azonic.co.nz> wrote innews:730ebdde-cade-4b3a-95c4-9b234bdeef1f@i10g2000pbc.googlegroups.com:
>
…[28 more quoted lines elided]…
> But you can't tell that, because you're using Google to try to read newsgroups.

Google Groups uses "Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable".
With this encoding (and others) an "=" is placed in position
76 of longer lines and the line is split. The 'mangling' occurs
at these points.

I notice that you are using "User-Agent: Xnews/2006.08.24".

< http://xnews.newsguy.com/release/changes.txt >
-----
4.05.03:

o Fixed a couple of quoted-printable decoding bugs.
-----

Perhaps an upgrade is in order.
```

HansJ wrote:
> On 22 Feb., 03:47, "Pete Dashwood"
> <dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
…[53 more quoted lines elided]…
> Regards Hans

There is always a risk if you post publicly (even if you use a pseudonynm)

If you are honest, upfront, and use your own name, then people can certainly 
find you.

(It is no accident that I live on a remote island at the end of the world... 
:-))

If you don't use your own name (which is sensible) then you are open to the 
criticism that you are not upfront, and you don't have the right to be 
critical because the people you are criticising should have a right to face 
their accuser.

So, if you want to be able to say whatever you like, you probably should 
post under your own name and be prepared to back what you said.

If you are afraid that someone might knife you for what you want to say, 
then it might be wise to think again. On the other hand if you think it is 
absolutely imperative that you make your thoughts known, and to Hell with 
the consequences, then go ahead. Only you can make that call for you.

You say the Islamic stuff is "more than just bugging you", Hans.

I understand how you feel; over the years I have seen stuff here that bugged 
me immensely (and it was nothing to do with Islam).

When you start to feel like that it is important to get things back in 
perspective.

It is just a newsgroup. Some people will misuse it, but the majority won't. 
And does it really matter?

You know very well the kind of person who posts that kind of rubbish. If you 
heard someone in the street propounding the same dogma you'd probably cross 
the road. So why let them get to you here?

Remember that YOU are responsible for how you feel; if you get seriously 
upset because some tunnel-visioned zealot wound you up, it is up to you to 
deal with it. Recognise it for what it is; trivia in the background noise.

(I can think of a number of occasions when I was very upset by exchanges 
here. Usually a walk down the beach and  a beer made me realise I was being 
stupid to get upset by a Usenet Forum.)

Definitely, stop accessing through Google Groups and get yourself some more 
selective access where they filter the rabid crap out and you have some 
control over what you see and respond to.

Perspective is everything when you are upset.

Pete.
```

### Strange file (2)

- **From:** drop dead google <foodman123@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-02-21T04:13:05-08:00

- **Message-ID:** `<b7462d33-99ae-48e9-b8d8-091e712ba88d@ge5g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>`

```
Hello:

Rather than respond to individual posts, here is a response to
everything
(Except the usual and expected childish wisecracks and other
sarcastic,
insulting, or pedantic comments which reflect poorly on the maturity,
intelligence
and professionalism of some CLC members.)

The compiler is Micro-Focus version 5. Windows XP.

The program compiles and links with no errors.

Yes, the file is closed before calling the other program.

My program executes 16 writes.

BRIEF shows 16 records.

I have been programming for more than 52 years now and in all that
time
I never had occasion to use a Hex editor but I found one which also
shows
16 records. Characters 101-4100 contain 00 as Richard correctly
guessed.

Doug Miller said "Why would you expect it to behave differently?"
The reason I tried it on another PC is because the EXE uses other
things
which could conceivably be bad - albeit highly unlikely.  I only
emailed
the EXE since the other things were already on the receiving PC.
Worth a try, don't you agree?.

Alistair questioned whether the 16 and 256 were coincidences.
Sure is some coincidence if they are.  There must be some sort of
clue here.

Dashwood said "It seems pretty obvious to me that this could be
easily solved with a Hex editor...".  A Hex editor can only
SHOW you the data, not HOW it got there.   Would you like me
to email the file to you so that you can show us how the problem
would be 'easily solved' by the use of a Hex editor, Dashwood?

Richard said "Tony obviously doesn't know how problems could be
diagnosed. "
So, here's the code, Richard, teach me how.

The relevant code is shown below. Every statement referencing the file
is shown.  The essence of this simple code was written in 1986 and has
been
used hundreds of times.

           SELECT SPULE        ASSIGN TO
DISK,
                               ORGANIZATION IS LINE SEQUENTIAL,
                               FILE STATUS IS W-FSTAT.


       FD   SPULE     DATA RECORD IS SPULE-PA,
                      LABEL RECORDS ARE STANDARD,
                      VALUE OF FILE-ID IS 'PRINT.SPL'.
       01   SPULE-PA  PIC X(100).



       WR.
           OPEN OUTPUT SPULE.   (File status is zero after open).


       WR15.

           MOVE SPACE  TO SPULE-PA.
           STRING ' ', DM-RUNNER '  ' DM-OCC-CODE '  ',
                   DM-MO '/' DM-DY '/' DM-YR, '   ' WZ2 ':'
                   DM-MIN-IN '   ' WZ22 ':' DM-MIN-OUT '  '
                   WZ-HRS ':' WZ-MINS '  ' WZ-RATE  WZ-GROSS
                       DELIMITED BY SIZE INTO SPULE-PA.
           PERFORM W1AS.



       WR200.
           CLOSE SPULE.        (File status is zero after close).



       W1AS.
           ADD 1 TO LINCT.
           WRITE SPULE-PA.     (File status is zero after write).
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Strange file (2)

- **From:** SkippyPB <swiegand@Nospam.neo.rr.com>

```
On Wed, 22 Feb 2012 03:17:59 +1300, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:

>drop dead google wrote:
>> Hello:
…[159 more quoted lines elided]…
>Pete.

I'd like to help out here but as Pete and Richard have said, you
haven't supplied enough of the program to do a proper debug/diagnosis.
Line Sequential is a Micro Focus implementation that supports a
standard text file layout.  That means that all trailing spaces are
removed at the time the record is written.

Your hex editor showed nulls in the trailing positions.  So either you
the compiler you are using doesn't recognize LINE SEQUENTIAL or you've
inadvertantly created a record larger than what your 01 Level says it
is.  

The old way of creating records in Working-Storage and writing them
from there so as not to mess with output buffers would seem to be
important here.   In addition, since we don't know the length of the
fields you are "stringing", conjecture is the best you are going to
get from the denizens of this newsgroup.

Regards,
```

#### ↳ Re: Strange file (2)

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-02-21T09:37:12-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<90fc6160-556f-44c5-9b00-bc6d79978c11@n4g2000pbl.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<b7462d33-99ae-48e9-b8d8-091e712ba88d@ge5g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Feb 22, 1:13 am, drop dead google <foodman...@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hello:
>
…[80 more quoted lines elided]…
>            WRITE SPULE-PA.     (File status is zero after write).

You had said that you expected the data of the record to be 100
characters. Given that you haven't supplied the lengths relevant to
the string operation this may give the actual 100.

With a line sequential the trailing spaces will be removed and a CR/LF
added. You haven't supplied room for this. It is possible that there
is an issue with this particular compiler version when there is no
room for the terminator to be added. The program would then write out
the complete block buffer which contains nulls for the remainder.

The solution/avoidance is probably to make the record area larger:

        01   SPULE-PA  PIC X(256).

Some experimentation with various sizes may show that this particualar
Microfocus version has a bug when the last character of the record is
non-space.
```

On Feb 22, 1:13 am, drop dead google <foodman...@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hello:
>
…[23 more quoted lines elided]…
> guessed.

One further complication with MF LINE SEQUENTIAL files is that there
is a run time switch: N - NULL Insertion; that changes the behaviour.

Depending on the N switch (I can't remember if this is on or off) it
will insert a null character before any control character (less than
space). On reading the NULL will be stripped when the N switch is the
same way.

This may also be related to the bug. Try running the program as it is
with the N switch off and again with it on.


> Doug Miller said "Why would you expect it to behave differently?"
> The reason I tried it on another PC is because the EXE uses other
…[18 more quoted lines elided]…
> So, here's the code, Richard, teach me how.

It wasn't about how or whether _you_ could diagnose the problem, you
had already told us that you could not.

It was about how you could expect us to diagnose it for you with
inadequate information supplied. If you understood how diagnosis could
be done you would have supplied sufficient in the first message.

For example the compiler version tells me about how LINE SEQUENTIAL is
implemented. MF has various switches which affect the processing (N,
T). Fujitsu has CBR_TRAILING_BLANK_RECORD. Other compilers may have
other variations.

The source code, that you provided some of now, almost tells us that
the record area is full.

> The relevant code is shown below. Every statement referencing the file
> is shown.  The essence of this simple code was written in 1986 and has
…[31 more quoted lines elided]…

Tony
It has been a while since I used MicroFocus so bear with me.
First. I assume that Pete’s reference to hex editor was to see if
there is any code other than nulls that could be causing the problem.
If the problem is caused by nulls, put in a line with using the
inspect replacing x”00” by spaces. That would remove the nulls from an
issue.
Second. Change the file type from “.SPL” to “.TXT”. I remember windows
and MicroFocus “helping” with some specific file types. This may be
one.
Third. Your are on the right track. If you have a small program that
works and large one that does not rip out code till it works. Then the
problem will be obvious.

When you find it please post the answer I would like to know.
Good luck.

Tom

> diagnose the problem, you had already told us that you could not."

I didn't quote you at all. It wasn't a quote, that would have been set
in quotation marks, it was a summary of your messages.

> I did not say that I "could not" solve the problem in my original post
> nor would I have said that.  I said "Any ideas anyone?"

Whether you said that you could not is irrelevant, you could not and
have not.

But the comment was not about you not diagnosing, it was expecting us
to diagnose based on a lack of adequate data, and even incorrect
information.


> Obviously there is something wrong. It may even be a compiler or
> linker
> bug which only arises in a specific set of circumstances.
>
> I wrote a tiny program containing the posted code and it works fine.

> There is must be something else being executed which is causing the
> problem.
> I can remove chunks of code in an attempt to narrow the problem down.

It is possible that it is the SP2. Check that the generated code
included is a correct match for the panel file being used. Also check
that the panel file is not larger than 1 megabyte. In fact rebuild the
panel file to compact it, if it gets too large then strange things
happen.

Turn on bounds checking to see if it is a corruption from an invalid
index value.
```

<a id="t-fccf7b9df0"></a>
## Thread: Relevance of COBOL — 21 this month / 27 total

### Relevance of COBOL

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-02-24T00:10:08+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9qml4hF42tU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
About 3 years ago I wrote an article about the relevance of COBOL.

Quite a bit has changed since then, including my own views, which have 
exanded in the light of experience.

This article is about to be presented to an audience of people who have 
COBOL as part of their organisations and the group will consist of various 
Analysts, Managers, and even Programmers...:-) from various companies.

(The companies are mainly Small/Medium businesses and they are in various 
parts of the World).

The document is not finalised yet but I'm releasing it to this group as a 
preview... Exclusive!! You saw it here first! :-)

I am conscious that I am close to the subject and I want to make sure I 
treat it fairly.

My goals are as follows:

1. Make a fair statement about the future of COBOL. (This, of course, is 
entirely a matter of opinion and completely arguable; nevertheless, I 
present my own thoughts on it.)
2. Examine some of the options that are available for dealing with the COBOL 
legacy. Obviously, I would like people to use the PRIMA Toolset, (which 
allows you to retain COBOL as your development language if you want to, 
although I cannot, in all conscience, recommend that) but that is not the 
primary thrust of the article. It is much more important to get people 
engaged in thinking about legacy and discussing it.

The article does not deal with moving to Solaris or Linux, although these 
are also increasinglyy important target platforms. It is aimed at people who 
are committed to the Windows environment and .Net.

If you think there are points I have missed or anything in the article is 
unfair, please post here. Send the article link below to people you know who 
have an interest in COBOL.

If good points come back, I'll amend the article. Remember you saw it here 
first...:-)

As always, I have checked the web coding in Chrome, Firefox, and IE (Chrome 
moves the 'Home' link but otherwise renders OK...) so if you have any 
problems viewing, please let me know about that too...

I can promise you that no attempt is made to track anyone accessing and all 
accesses are completely anonymous. No cookies, no adware, nada...

http://primacomputing.co.nz/cobol21/COBOLRelevance.aspx

Thanks in advance for your help,

Pete.
```

```
Alistair Maclean wrote:
> On Feb 24, 3:49 pm, Kerry Liles
> <"kerry.liles[minus_the_spam]"@gmail.com> wrote:
…[109 more quoted lines elided]…
> meter stick is US English. Over here we use metre sticks.

Somewhere in the timewarp which is my garage, I have a 36 inch piece of wood 
called a "yardstick".

I can't see me ever getting my head around "metre stick", although I have no 
difficulty with the metric system in other areas.

Whether "meter stick" is American or not, it makes slightly more sense 
because "meter" comes from a root meaning simply "to measure" (hence meters 
and gauges) and a "meter stick" would then simply be a "measuring stick", 
that might not be 1 metre long but could be any unit you wanted it to be.

Having been raised on imperial measurements I still find it hard to 
immediately visualise say, 5 cm, but if someone says "6 inches" or a "foot" 
the mental image is immediate. There is no question in my mind that the 
Metric system is better for everyday use; I just wish it had been drilled 
into me in school... Having said all of that, I'd still have difficulty 
visualizing "3 pennyweight"  or "half a hogshead"... but no trouble with "6 
furlongs" (I enjoy a day at the Races, although the official distances are 
now in metres), "1 chain" (the length of a cricket pitch), or "1 
hundredweight" the weight of a bag of coal in the old days.

I've heard old-timers protesting that the World is being dumbed down but the 
Metric system is simply more efficient. Because I buy 500 grams of butter 
and 2 litres of milk repeatedly, there is no problem with visualizing these 
units and I would struggle now to visualize a pound of butter or a quart of 
milk.

But I won't be relinquishing the use of "yardstick" as a benchmarking tool 
any time soon...

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: Relevance of COBOL

- **From:** Alistair Maclean <alistair.j.l.maclean@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-02-23T13:22:55-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<69e571c1-5031-43ed-b545-c8980d5221e5@i2g2000vbv.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<9qml4hF42tU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
On Feb 23, 11:10 am, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
> About 3 years ago I wrote an article about the relevance of COBOL.
>
…[38 more quoted lines elided]…
>

You already know where I live so cookies ain't a problem.

Pete, you have some inconcistencies (you refer to Micro Focus Cli but
Fujitsur CLI) and poor English (one of my favourites is that people
don't jump off bridges but they jump off of bridges and something like
the former appears in the article). More serious issues:

1. Why change COBOL systems at all, if they work and if their staff
are familiar with the codebase?

2. Why change the COBOL version when the data manager can bask in the
glory of being the first script kiddie on the block to re-write all of
his systems in Java or C# and expose his team and company to the
cutting edge of technology and an inflated maintenance burden?

3. You argue that a COBOL file layout does not an efficient relational
database make (says Yoda) but you are offering your toolset to do
exactly that. Now I know that you refer to TNF but I doubt if your
clients know what that is and why they should use or avoid it (I
prefer LDST).

4. If your clients jump to use the toolset then they may be faced with
excessive immediate maintenance burdens as they learn the new
codebase.

Good luck, cobber.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Relevance of COBOL

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-02-24T13:03:17+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9qo2e2Fd12U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<9qml4hF42tU1@mid.individual.net> <69e571c1-5031-43ed-b545-c8980d5221e5@i2g2000vbv.googlegroups.com>`

```
Alistair Maclean wrote:
> On Feb 23, 11:10 am, "Pete Dashwood"
> <dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
…[50 more quoted lines elided]…
> the former appears in the article).

Thanks. As always I want the standard of English to be as good as I can 
write so I will proof it again. The inconsistencies are no problem but it 
would be really helpful if you could quote the redundant preposition.

More serious issues:
>
> 1. Why change COBOL systems at all, if they work and if their staff
> are familiar with the codebase?

Because there is need of a different paradigm for networked systems. Was 
that not clear? Staff are extremely important but a company cannot tie its 
capability to the "comfort" of its employees. I strongly recommend that 
investment is made in training. One of the reasons for this article is to 
get programmers thinking about what they need to learn and why. It isn't 
about bullying people to become better qualified, but it isn't about 
accepting complacency either.
>
> 2. Why change the COBOL version when the data manager can bask in the
> glory of being the first script kiddie on the block to re-write all of
> his systems in Java or C# and expose his team and company to the
> cutting edge of technology and an inflated maintenance burden?

Some people are finding that when they move to OO COBOL it is not as good as 
if they had gone directly to an OO language. Nevertheless, I think that OO 
COBOL IS useful and it is a good transition experience for COBOL guys to get 
used to the concepts. Your comment about an inflated maintenance burden is 
just nonsens so I'll ignore it :-)

(Oh, and BTW, until you actually learn to write scripts and realise how 
useful they are, you should not dismiss this ability.)
>
> 3. You argue that a COBOL file layout does not an efficient relational
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> prefer LDST).

Not quite. A COBOL layout CAN be quite efficient on a database but it is 
when OCCURS, REDEFINES, Group Fields, and DATE types are included that 
things get a little sticky. I spent months manually transferring COBOL 
records into RDB and refining and improving the necessary DDL until I could 
get a set of rules that was programmable. I then encapsulated that 
experience into the Toolset. In practise, it doesn't matter whether people 
use the PRIMA toolset or do it manually, normalization still leads to a 
better Database.

My clients do know about Normalizing RDBs and if they don't, I provide 
documentation which clearly and simply explains it and have run the odd 
afternoon seminar covering it.

(The COBOL21 site also has such information available and over 3000 people 
have downloaded or browsed it. In fact, the SQL part of the site is 
something I should update as there is a steady stream of hits on it.  There 
is a paper on RDBMS Normalization at:

http://primacomputing.co.nz/cobol21/SQL.aspx

I just looked at this page and realized it is not rendering correctly in IE; 
I'll fix it later today.)

When people start to get interested in a "new" (to them...) technology, they 
usually do some homework and the concept of normalization is part of that. I 
don't believe everyone using a RDBMS needs to fully understand the 
mathematical implications of Codd's Relational Model, but Normalization is 
not hard to cope with.
>
> 4. If your clients jump to use the toolset then they may be faced with
> excessive immediate maintenance burdens as they learn the new
> codebase.

There isn't a "new codebase". There is an existing Legacy codebase that has 
been transformed to have all ISAM access replaced with invokes of a DAL 
object. The Legacy code continues to run exactly as it always has, but now 
it has a new datasource. Instead of the old ISAM files, it uses the newly 
defined RDB.

It would be quite feasible (although no-one has actually done this because 
it hasn't proved necessary) to keep the old ISAM version of your legacy 
programs (people normally archive this anyway) and continue maintaining that 
just as you always have. Change a program, run it through Transformation in 
the Toolset (a matter of seconds) and your new changes are reflected in a 
program that is accessing the new database. The Toolset generates working 
code in seconds and the generated code has already been debugged.

The DAL objects are generated by the Toolset also and they enable the legacy 
to use the new Database. New development (which can be in any OO Language 
(including COBOL) MAY use the DAL objects as a convenient way to manipulate 
legacy record formats, but it doesn't HAVE to.

I have deliberately kept the DAL methods similar to what COBOL programmers 
are used to when they write programs to access ISAM files. There is a DAL 
programming handbook which shows how you can use these objects to get access 
to your legacy COBOL record formats from the new RDB and it means you can 
access your existing COBOL data from a web page or a desktop just by 
instantiating the appropriate DAL object. (and invoking its methods... :-))

http://primacomputing.co.nz/cobol21/PRIMAToolset.aspx  (click the link near 
the bottom of the page to browse the DAL programming manual. The 
introduction explains what it is.)


Legacy programs require to have the COBOL record, but new programs may 
access a subset of columns or a join or a view just as is usual with 
Relational DB programming. ALL of the access, old and new, is separated to 
the Data Access Layer.

Usually, when people are looking at conversion and migration, they get the 
legacy system as stable as they can so it doesn't require much maintenance 
and they are focussing on new development against the new RDB. The DAL 
objects allow the legacy to participate alongside the new development and 
everything works of the same production RDB. (An immediate benefit of this 
is that there is no longer any need to synchronise the Legacy system data 
with the new RDB on a daily basis).

Experience has shown there is no "excessive" learning curve for legacy 
programmers.

>
> Good luck, cobber.

Thanks, it is amazing how lucky I get when I work hard... :-)

Pete.
```

On Feb 24, 1:03 pm, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
> Alistair Maclean wrote:
> > On Feb 23, 11:10 am, "Pete Dashwood"
…[24 more quoted lines elided]…
> >> nevertheless, I present my own thoughts on it.)

The future of all languages should be reviewed. Many fall by the
wayside as they are replaced by newer, more trendy, languages. At one
time many accounting systems were written in various dialects of
BASIC. Then Pascal or derivatives such as Delphi.

At some point Java and C# may become 'legacy' or obsolete.


> >> 2. Examine some of the options that are available for dealing with
> >> the COBOL legacy. Obviously, I would like people to use the PRIMA
…[38 more quoted lines elided]…
> capability to the "comfort" of its employees.

There is no particular reason that COBOL cannot be used for 'networked
systems'. I have over the last quarter century used COBOL for web
based and AJAX systems, for Windows GUI (actual graphics drawing) for
client-server, for web-services.

Granted I use python for most stuff now, but COBOL can still work.

It isn't that COBOL can't be used for networked systems but that
mainframe based batch processing on ISAM files can't easily be
transitioned.

It may seem easier to replace these systems if COBOL and all the
programmers are thrown out and a clean slate using a new language
(where you would propose C# no doubt) were started.

> I strongly recommend that
> investment is made in training. One of the reasons for this article is to
> get programmers thinking about what they need to learn and why. It isn't
> about bullying people to become better qualified, but it isn't about
> accepting complacency either.

So you don't want to throw out the programmers you want to train them
to correct their thinking.

> > 2. Why change the COBOL version when the data manager can bask in the
> > glory of being the first script kiddie on the block to re-write all of
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> just nonsens so I'll ignore it :-)

Many years ago there was a Datamation article that surveyed various
software houses looking at the languages used and the 'maintenance'
burden.

It found that in COBOL shops there was something like 60% maintenance
and 40% new development, but in C shops there was 90% new development
and only 10% maintenance. The conclusion was: Rewrite all the COBOL
into C and save half your programming costs.

It was a complete fail. The COBOL shops were writing in-house
applications and the 'maintenance' was to adapt the systems to
changing business needs. The C shops were writing completely different
types of applications where the maintenance was purely of the bug
fixing nature and enhancements were in the 'new development'. If the
COBOL applications were rewritten to C (or Java or C#) they would
still be 60# maintenance because that was an attribute of the
application and the businesses, not of the language.

> (Oh, and BTW, until you actually learn to write scripts and realise how
> useful they are, you should not dismiss this ability.)

Well, geez, Pete, nearly 30 years ago I wrote a 'synthetic system' in
COBOL, originally for CP/M. This allowed me to set up screens to
maintain data files, to produce reports, CSV files, and enquiries, all
with scripts.  The scripts are simple and allow me to get a report out
in just a few minutes.  This system is still in use and has been added
to over the years.

It may be that there are COBOL programmers that are stuck in the same
development environment that they had in the 70s but that is not the
fault of the COBOL language.


> > 3. You argue that a COBOL file layout does not an efficient relational
> > database make (says Yoda) but you are offering your toolset to do
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> things get a little sticky.

Especially when you also get multiple record types in one file, such
as would be useful on tape based systems, or when there were limits on
how many files could be open at one time.

But that is a matter that can be fixed by redeveloping the file
system. If that hasn't been done as the facility to do it has improved
then the problem is not the language but the culture of being stuck in
the past.


> I spent months manually transferring COBOL
> records into RDB and refining and improving the necessary DDL until I could
…[85 more quoted lines elided]…
> "I used to write COBOL...now I can do anything."
```

> At one
> time many accounting systems were written in various dialects of
> BASIC. Then Pascal or derivatives such as Delphi.

Yes, but modern accounting systems have more functionality and that is the 
nub of it all. By using Classes the systems become more modular and that 
means newer functionality can be more readily added and existing 
functionality can be more easily reused in other systems which may not 
strictly be "accounting " systems.

> At some point Java and C# may become 'legacy' or obsolete.

Undoubtedly. But at the moment, they embrace the Object Paradigm and that is

have.)

It is interesting that despite both of us having worked for many years with 
COBOL, today  it is not a preferred solution for either of us. I like C#, 
you use Python. Both of these languages do not have the verbosity of COBOL 
and both of them support Objects better than COBOL does.

>I have over the last quarter century used COBOL for web
> based and AJAX systems, for Windows GUI (actual graphics drawing) for
> client-server, for web-services.

> It isn't that COBOL can't be used for networked systems but that
> mainframe based batch processing on ISAM files can't easily be
> transitioned.

Well, yes and no.

Although I'm not currently offering a solution to mainframe sites, the 
reason for that has more to do with the frugal facilities for compiling 
Objects in the mainframe environment than it does with any innate 
difficulties in the file system. I can create a normalized database from 
VSAM/KSDS datasets just as easily as I can from ISAM datasets on a PC. What 
I cannot do (currently) is provide DAL support. (And it isn't impossible; it 
is just more work than I'm prepared to do at the moment.) I COULD provide 
procedural code modules that would provide a Data Access Layer and could be 
called from existing Legacy code just as DAL objects are invoked from it, 
but I haven't had occasion to do so and it is a fair bit of work to make the 
Toolset generate non-OO Code. There is no more work in transforming 
mainframe COBOL than there is in Transforming PC COBOL so that is not a 
problem. I don't have access to a mainframe site at the moment and I'm not 
prpared to buy access unless there is a customer for the migration.
>

## Thread: MAJOR CANADIAN CHRISTIAN MISSIONARY CONVERTS TO ISLAM !!!!!!!!!!!!!! — 17 this month / 39 total

### MAJOR CANADIAN CHRISTIAN MISSIONARY CONVERTS TO ISLAM !!!!!!!!!!!!!!

- **From:** BV <cv33cv33cv33@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-02-26T00:20:31-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c4c37650-16b0-4dda-b312-88220278d8d2@w5g2000vbv.googlegroups.com>`

```
MAJOR CANADIAN CHRISTIAN MISSIONARY CONVERTS TO ISLAM
By: Dr Garry Miller:
A very important Christian missionary converted to Islam and became a
major herald for Islam, he was a very active missionary and was very
knowledgeable about the Bible...

This man likes mathematics so much, that's why he likes logic. One
day, he decided to read the Quran to try to find any mistakes that he
might take advantage of while inviting Muslims to convert to
Christianity.... He expected the Koran to be an old book written 14
centuries ago, a book that talks about the desert and so on...He was
amazed from what he found. He discovered that this Book had what no
other book in the world has.... He expected to find some stories about
the hard time that the Prophet Mohammad (Peace Be Upon Him) had, like
the death of his wife Khadijah (may Allah be pleased with her) or the
death of his sons and daughters...however, he did not find anything
like that... and what made him even more confused is that he found a
full "sura"(chapter) in the Koran named "Mary" that contains a lot of
respect to Mary(peace be upon her) which is not the case even in the
books written by Christians nor in their bibles.
He did not find a Sura named after "Fatimah"(the prophet's daughter)
nor "Aa’ishah"(the Prophet's wife), may Allah(God) be pleased with
both of them. He also found that the name of Jesus(Peace Be Upon Him)
was mentioned in the Koran 25 times while the name of "Mohammed"(Peace
Be Upon Him) was mentioned only 4 times, so he became more confused.
He started reading the Koran more thoroughly hoping to find a mistake
but he was shocked when he read a great verse which is verse number 82
in Surat Al-Nisa'(Women) that says:

“Do they not consider the Koran (with care)? Had it been from other
than Allah, they would surely have found therein much discrepancy”.

Dr Miller says about this verse: “ One of the well known scientific
principles is the principle of finding mistakes or looking for
mistakes in a theory until it’s proved to be right (Falsification Test)
…what’s amazing is that the Holy Quran asks Muslims and non-muslims to
try to find mistakes in this book and it tells them that they will
never find any”. He also says about this verse: no writer in the world
has the courage to write a book and say that it’s empty of mistakes,
but the Quran, on the contrary, tells you that it has no mistakes and
asks you to try to find one and you won’t find any.

Another verse that Dr Miller reflected on for a long time is the verse
number 30 in Surat “Al-Anbiya’”(The Prophets): “ Do not the
Unbelievers see that the heavens and the earth were joined together
(as one unit of Creation), before We clove them asunder? We made from
water every living thing. Will they not then believe?”

He says: “ This verse is exactly the subject of the scientific
research that won the Noble prize in 1973 and was about the theory of
the “Great Explosion”. According to this theory, the universe was the
result of a great explosion that leads to the formation of the
universe with its skies and planets”.

Dr Miller says: “ Now we come to what’s amazing about the Prophet
Mohammed (PBUH) and what’s pretended about the devils helping him, God
says: “No evil ones have brought down this (Revelation), it would
neither suit them nor would they be able (to produce it). Indeed they
have been removed far from even (a chance of) hearing
it” (26:210-212). “When thou do read the Quran, seek Allah's
protection from Satan the Rejected One” (16:98).

You see? can this be the devil’s way to write a book? how can he write
a book then tells you to ask God for protection from this devil before
reading that book? those are miraculous verses in this miraculous
book! and has a logical answer to those who pretend that it’s from the
devil”. And among the stories that amazed Dr Miller is the story of
the Prophet (PBUH) with Abu-Lahab… Dr Miller says: “ This man (Abu
Lahab) used to hate Islam so much that he would go after the Prophet
wherever he goes to humiliate him. If he saw the prophet talking to
strangers, he used to wait till he finishes and then ask them: what
did Mohammed tell you? If he said it’s white then it’s in reality
black and if he said it’s night then it’s day. He meant to falsify all
what the prophet says and to make people suspicious about it. And 10
years before the death of Abu Lahab, a sura was inspired to the
prophet, named “Al-Masad”. This sura tells that Abu Lahab will go to
hell, in other words, it says that Abu Lahab will not convert to
Islam. During 10 years, Abu Lahab could have said: “Mohammed is saying
that I will not become a Muslim and that I will go to the hell fire,
but I’m telling you now that I want to convert to Islam and become a
Muslim. What do you think about Mohammed now? Is he saying the truth
or no? Does his inspiration come from God?”
But Abu Lahab did not do that at all although he was disobeying the
prophet in all matters, but not in this one. In other words, it was as
if the prophet (PBUH) was giving Abu Lahab a chance to prove him
wrong! But he did not do that during 10 whole years! he did not
convert to Islam and did not even pretend to be a Muslim!! Throughout
10 years, he had the chance to destroy Islam in 1 minute! But this did
not happen because those are not the words of Mohammed (PBUH) but the
words of God Who knows what’s hidden and knows that Abu Lahab will not
become a Muslim.

How can the prophet (PBUH) know that Abu Lahab will prove what is said
in that Sura if this was not inspiration from Allah? How can he be
sure throughout 10 whole years that what he has (the Quran) is true if
he did not know that it’s inspiration from Allah?? For a person to
take such a risky challenge, this has only one meaning: that this is
inspiration from God.

“Perish the hands of the Father of Flame (Abu Lahab)! perish he! No
profit to him from all his wealth, and all his gains! Burnt soon will
he be in a Fire of blazing Flame! His wife shall carry the (crackling)
wood; As fuel! A twisted rope of palm-leaf fibre round her (own)
neck!” (surat Al-Masad).

Dr Miller says about a verse that amazed him: one of the miracles in
the Quran is challenging the future with things that humans cannot
predict and to which the “Falsification Test” applies, this test
consists of looking for mistakes until the thing that is being tested
is proved to be right. For example, let’s see what the Quran said
about the relation between Muslims and Jews. Quran says that Jews are
the major enemies for Muslims and this is true until now as the main
enemy for Muslims are the Jews.

Dr Miller continues: this is considered a great challenge since the
Jews have the chance to ruin Islam simply by treating Muslims in a
friendly way for few years and then say: here we are treating you as
friends and the Quran says that we are your enemies, the Quran must be
wrong then! But this did not happen during 1400 years!! and it will
never happen because those are the words of The One who knows the
unseen (God) and not the words of humans.

Dr Miller continues: can you see how the verse that talks about the
enmity between Muslims and Jews constitutes a challenge to the human
mind? “Strongest among men in enmity to the Believers wilt thou find
the Jews and Pagans; and nearest among them in love to the Believers
wilt thou find those who say, "We are Christians": because amongst
these are men devoted to learning and men who have renounced the
world, and they are not arrogant. And when they listen to the
revelation received by the Messenger, thou wilt see their eyes
overflowing with tears, for they recognize the truth: they pray: "Our
Lord! We believe; write us down among the witnesses” (5: 82-84)

This verse applies to Dr Miller as he was a Christian but when he knew
the truth, he believed and converted to Islam and became a herald. May
Allah support him.

Dr Miller says about the unique style of the Quran that he finds
wonderful: no doubt there is something unique and amazing in Quran
that is not present anywhere else, as the Quran gives you specific
information and tells you that you did not know this before. For
example: "This is part of the tidings of the things unseen, which We
reveal unto thee (O Prophet!) by inspiration: thou was not with them
when they cast lots with arrows, as to which of them should be charged
with the care of Maryam: nor was thou with them when they disputed
(the point)” (3: 44).

“Such are some of the stories of the Unseen, which We have revealed
unto thee: before this, neither thou nor thy People knew them. So
persevere patiently: for the End is for those who are righteous” (11:
49). “Such is one of the stories of what happened unseen, which We
reveal by inspiration unto thee: nor was thou (present) with them when
they concerted their plans together in the process of weaving their
plots” (12: 102)

Dr Miller continues: “ No other holy book uses this style, all the
other books consist of information that tells you where this
information came from. For example, when the (distorted) holy bible
talks about the stories of the ancient nations, it tells you that a
this king lived in a this place and a that leader fought in that
battle, and that a certain person had a number of kids and their names
are…. But this book (distorted Bible) always tells you that if you
want to know more, you can read a certain book since that information
came from that book”.

Dr Garry Miller continues: “this is in contrary to the Quran which
gives you the information and tells you that it’s new!! And what’s
amazing is that the people of Mecca at that time -time of inspiration
of those verses- used to hear those verses and the challenge that the
information in those verses was new and was not known by Mohammed
(PBUH) nor by his people at that time, and despite that, they never
said: we know this and it is not new, and they did not say: we know
where Mohammed came from with those verses. This never happened, but
what happened is that nobody dared to say that he was lying to them
because those was really new information, not coming from the human
mind but from Allah who knows the unseen in the past, the present and
the future”.

May Allah reward Dr Miller for this nice reflection on the Book of
Allah
